<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Big Ten Conference</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p>The <b>Big Ten Conference</b> (<b>B1G</b>), formerly <b>Western Conference</b> and <b>Big Nine Conference</b>, is the oldest Division I collegiate <a href="/wiki/List_of_NCAA_conferences" title="List of NCAA conferences">athletic conference</a> in the United States. The conference, consisting of 14 members as of 2016, competes in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a>; its <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a> teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision">Football Bowl Subdivision</a> (FBS), formerly known as Division I-A, the highest level of NCAA competition in that sport. The conference includes the flagship public university in each of 11 states stretching from New Jersey to Nebraska, as well as two additional public land grant schools and a private university.</p>
<p>The Big Ten Conference was established in 1895 when <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a> president James H. Smart and representatives from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois" title="University of Illinois">University of Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin" title="University of Wisconsin">University of Wisconsin</a> gathered at Chicago's Palmer House Hotel to set policies aimed at regulating intercollegiate athletics. In 1905, the conference was officially incorporated as the "Intercollegiate Conference Athletic Association".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Big Ten member institutions are predominantly major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagship_university" title="Flagship university">flagship</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_universities" title="Research universities">research universities</a> with large financial endowments and strong academic reputations. Large student enrollment is also a hallmark of Big Ten universities, as 12 of the 14 members feature enrollments of 30,000 or more students. <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>, one of just two full members with a total enrollment of fewer than 30,000 students (the other is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska%E2%80%93Lincoln" title="University of Nebraska–Lincoln">University of Nebraska–Lincoln</a>), is the lone <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private university</a> among Big Ten membership (the University of Chicago, a private university, left the conference in 1946). Collectively, Big Ten universities educate more than 520,000 total students and have 5.7 million living alumni.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigten.org_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-bigten.org-2">[2]</a></sup> Big Ten universities engage in $9.3 billion in funded research each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Though the Big Ten existed for nearly a century as an assemblage of universities located primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a>, the conference's geographic footprint now spans from the state of <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a> in the west to the Atlantic Ocean in the east.</p>
<p>Big Ten universities are also members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Academic_Alliance" title="Big Ten Academic Alliance">Big Ten Academic Alliance</a>, an academic <a href="/wiki/Consortium" title="Consortium">consortium</a>. In 2014–2015, members generated more than $10 billion in research expenditures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btaa_stats_2014_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-btaa_stats_2014-4">[4]</a></sup> Despite the conference's name, the Big Ten has grown to fourteen members, with the following universities accepting invitations to join: <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Pennsylvania State University</a> in 1990, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska%E2%80%93Lincoln" title="University of Nebraska–Lincoln">University of Nebraska–Lincoln</a> in 2011, and both the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University" title="Rutgers University">Rutgers University</a> in 2014. <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> was invited in 2012 to join the Big Ten as an associate member participating in men's <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a> only. In 2015, it was also accepted as an associate member in <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_lacrosse" title="Women's lacrosse">women's lacrosse</a>. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">Notre Dame</a> is scheduled to join the Big Ten in 2017 as an associate member in men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> was a co-founder of the conference.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lake_Forest_College" title="Lake Forest College">Lake Forest College</a> attended the original 1895 meeting that led to the formation of the conference, but did not join it.</li>
</ul>

<p>Notes:</p>
<p>* Notre Dame will join the Big Ten in the 2017–18 school year as an affiliate member in men's ice hockey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[10]</a></sup> It continues to field its other sports in the ACC except in football where it will continue to compete as an independent.</p>
<p>° Johns Hopkins joined the Big Ten in 2014 as an affiliate member in men's lacrosse, with women's lacrosse to follow in 2016. It continues to field its other sports in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">NCAA Division III</a> <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Conference" title="Centennial Conference">Centennial Conference</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B1GLax_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-B1GLax-18">[11]</a></sup></p>

<p>Notes:</p>
<p>1: Fencing is officially a coeducational team sport, although a few schools field only a women's team. Ohio State and Penn State, like most NCAA fencing schools, have coed teams.</p>
<p>2: Men's rowing, whether heavyweight or lightweight, is not governed by the NCAA, but instead by the <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a>. Rutgers Men's Rowing was downgraded to Club status in 2008, but remains a member of the EARC.</p>
<p>3: Unlike rifle, pistol is not an NCAA-governed sport. It is fully coeducational.</p>
<p>4: Rifle is technically a men's sport, but men's, women's, and coed teams all compete against each other. Ohio State fields a coed team.</p>

Nebraska fields a women-only team, and Ohio State fields a coed team.</span></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Initiated and led by Purdue University President James Henry Smart,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[12]</a></sup> the presidents of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois" title="University of Illinois">University of Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin" title="University of Wisconsin">University of Wisconsin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Forest_College" title="Lake Forest College">Lake Forest College</a> met in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> on January 11, 1895 to discuss the regulation and control of intercollegiate athletics. The eligibility of student-athletes was one of the main topics of discussion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-traditions_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-traditions-26">[13]</a></sup> The <b>Intercollegiate Conference of Faculty Representatives</b> was founded at a second meeting on February 8, 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Western_Conference_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Western_Conference-27">[14]</a></sup> Lake Forest was not at the 1896 meeting that established the conference and was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>. At the time, the organization was more commonly known as the <b>Western Conference</b>, consisting of Purdue, Michigan, Wisconsin, Minnesota, Illinois, Chicago, and Northwestern.</p>
<p>The first reference to the conference as the <b>Big Nine</b> was in 1899 after <a href="/wiki/University_of_Iowa" title="University of Iowa">Iowa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indiana_University_Bloomington" title="Indiana University Bloomington">Indiana</a> had joined. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska-Lincoln" title="University of Nebraska-Lincoln">Nebraska</a> first petitioned to join the league in 1900 and again in 1911,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huskerextra.com_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-huskerextra.com-28">[15]</a></sup> but was turned away both times. In April 1907, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">Michigan</a> was voted out of the conference for failing to adhere to league rules.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State</a> was added to the conference in 1912. The first known references to the conference as the <b>Big Ten</b> were in November 1917 after Michigan rejoined after a nine-year absence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conference was again known as the Big Nine after the University of Chicago decided to de-emphasize varsity athletics just after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Chicago discontinued its football program in 1939<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[20]</a></sup> and withdrew from the conference in 1946 after struggling to obtain victories in many conference matchups. It was believed that one of several schools, notably Pittsburgh, Nebraska, Michigan State, Marquette, Notre Dame, and Iowa State would replace Chicago at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[21]</a></sup> On May 20, 1949,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Western_Conference_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Western_Conference-27">[14]</a></sup> Michigan State ended the speculation by joining and the conference was again known as the Big Ten. The Big Ten's membership would remain unchanged for the next 40 years. The conference's official name throughout this period remained the Intercollegiate Conference of Faculty Representatives. It did not formally adopt the name <i>Big Ten</i> until 1987, when it was incorporated as a not-for-profit corporation.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990_expansion:_Penn_State">1990 expansion: Penn State</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1990 expansion: Penn State">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="76" data-file-width="153" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg/220px-Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg/330px-Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg/440px-Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Big_Ten_Conference_Logo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Big Ten logo (1990–2011). To reflect the addition of the 11th school, Pennsylvania State, the number 11 was disguised in the negative space of the "Big Ten" lettering.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1990, the Big Ten universities voted to expand the conference to 11 teams and extended an invitation to <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Pennsylvania State University</a>, which accepted it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[22]</a></sup> When Penn State joined in 1990, it was decided the conference would continue to be called the Big Ten, but its <a href="/wiki/Logo" title="Logo">logo</a> was modified to reflect the change; the number 11 was disguised in the <a href="/wiki/Negative_space" title="Negative space">negative space</a> of the traditionally blue "Big Ten" lettering.</p>
<p>Missouri showed interest in Big Ten membership after Penn State joined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[23]</a></sup> Around 1993, the league explored adding <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kansas" title="University of Kansas">Kansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri" title="University of Missouri">Missouri</a> and Rutgers or other potential schools, to create a 14-team league with two divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[24]</a></sup> These talks died when the <a href="/wiki/Big_Eight_Conference" title="Big Eight Conference">Big Eight Conference</a> merged with former <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Conference" title="Southwest Conference">Southwest Conference</a> members to create the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12</a>.</p>
<p>Following the addition of previously independent Penn State, efforts were made to encourage the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">University of Notre Dame</a>, at that time the last remaining non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Service_academies" title="US Service academies">service academy</a> independent, to join the league. Early in the 20th century, Notre Dame briefly considered official entry into the Big Ten but chose to retain its independent status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[25]</a></sup> However, in 1999, Notre Dame and the Big Ten entered into private negotiations concerning a possible membership that would include Notre Dame. Although Notre Dame's faculty senate endorsed the idea with a near-unanimous vote, the school's board of trustees decided against joining the conference. <a class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071220054555/http://www.mndaily.com/daily/1999/02/08/sports/irish/" rel="nofollow">[2]</a> Notre Dame subsequently joined the Atlantic Coast Conference in all sports except football, in which Notre Dame maintains its independent status as long as it plays at least five games per season against ACC opponents. This was believed to be the major stumbling block to Notre Dame joining the Big Ten, as Notre Dame wanted to retain its independent <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Football_on_NBC" title="Notre Dame Football on NBC">home game broadcasting contract</a> with <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports" title="NBC Sports">NBC Sports</a>, while the Big Ten insisted upon a full membership with no special exemptions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.932014_expansion:_Nebraska.2C_Maryland.2C_Rutgers">2010–2014 expansion: Nebraska, Maryland, Rutgers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2010–2014 expansion: Nebraska, Maryland, Rutgers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9314_Big_Ten_Conference_realignment" title="2010–14 Big Ten Conference realignment">2010–14 Big Ten Conference realignment</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="705" data-file-width="1067" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ac/Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png/300px-Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ac/Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png/450px-Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ac/Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png/600px-Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Big_Ten_Conference_Membership_Map_2017.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Locations of the Big Ten member institutions</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In December 2009, Big Ten Conference commissioner <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Delany" title="James Delany">Jim Delany</a> announced that the league was looking to expand in what would later be part of a nationwide trend as part of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932014_NCAA_conference_realignment" title="2010–2014 NCAA conference realignment">2010–2014 NCAA conference realignment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Expansion_101_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Expansion_101-39">[26]</a></sup> On June 11, 2010, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska-Lincoln" title="University of Nebraska-Lincoln">University of Nebraska</a> applied for membership in the Big Ten and was unanimously approved as the conference's 12th school, which became effective July 1, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[27]</a></sup> The conference retained the name "Big Ten." This led to the interesting result of the Big Ten consisting of twelve teams, and the Big 12 consisting of ten teams.</p>
<p>On September 1, Delany revealed the conference's divisional split, but noted that the division names would be announced later. Those division names, as well as the conferences new logo, were made public on December 13, 2010. For their new logo, the conference replaced the "hidden 11" logo with one that uses the "B1G" character combination in its branding. Delany did not comment on the logo that day, but it was immediately evident that the new logo would "allow fans to see 'BIG' and '10' in a single word."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[28]</a></sup> For the new division names, the Big Ten was unable to use geographic names, as used by the SEC, because they had rejected a geographic arrangement. Delany announced that the new divisions would be known as the "Legends Division" and "Leaders Division". In the Legends division were Iowa, Michigan, Michigan State, Minnesota, Nebraska and Northwestern. The Leaders division was composed of Illinois, Indiana, Ohio State, Penn State, Purdue and Wisconsin. Conference officials stated they had focused on creating competitive fairness rather than splitting by geographical location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[29]</a></sup> However, the new "Legends" and "Leaders" names were not met with enthusiasm. Some traditional rivals, including Ohio State and Michigan, were placed in separate divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[30]</a></sup> For the football season, each team played the others in its division, one "cross-over" rivalry game, and two rotating cross-divisional games. At the end of the regular season the two division winners met in a new <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Football_Championship_Game" title="Big Ten Football Championship Game">Big Ten Football Championship Game</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[31]</a></sup> The Legends and Leaders divisional alignment was in effect for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Big_Ten_Conference_football_season" title="2011 Big Ten Conference football season">2011</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Big_Ten_Conference_football_season" title="2012 Big Ten Conference football season">2012</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2013_Big_Ten_Conference_football_season" title="2013 Big Ten Conference football season">2013</a> football seasons.</p>
<p>On November 19, 2012, the University of Maryland's Board of Regents voted to withdraw from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a> and join the Big Ten as its 13th member effective on July 1, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[32]</a></sup> The Big Ten's Council of Presidents approved the move later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[33]</a></sup> One day later, Rutgers University of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">Big East</a> also accepted an offer for membership from the Big Ten as its 14th member school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 28, 2013, the Big Ten presidents and chancellors unanimously approved a divisional realignment that went into effect when Maryland and Rutgers joined in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_realignment_approved_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014_realignment_approved-48">[35]</a></sup> Under the new plan, the Legends and Leaders divisions were replaced with geographic divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_realignment_approved_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014_realignment_approved-48">[35]</a></sup> The West Division includes Illinois, Iowa, Minnesota, Nebraska, Northwestern, Purdue and Wisconsin (of which all but Purdue are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">Central Time Zone</a>), while the East Division includes Indiana, Maryland, Michigan, Michigan State, Ohio State, Penn State and Rutgers. The final issue in determining the new divisions was which of the two Indiana schools would be sent to the West; Purdue was chosen because its <a href="/wiki/West_Lafayette,_Indiana" title="West Lafayette, Indiana">West Lafayette</a> campus is geographically west of Indiana's home city of <a href="/wiki/Bloomington,_Indiana" title="Bloomington, Indiana">Bloomington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_divisions_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014_divisions-49">[36]</a></sup> In the current divisional alignment, the only protected cross-divisional rivalry game in football is <a href="/wiki/Old_Oaken_Bucket" title="Old Oaken Bucket">Indiana–Purdue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_realignment_approved_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-2014_realignment_approved-48">[35]</a></sup> As before, the two division winners play each other in the Big Ten Football Championship Game.</p>
<p>On June 3, 2013, the Big Ten announced the sponsorship of men's and women's lacrosse. For any conference to qualify for an automatic bid to the NCAA tournament, at least six member schools must play the sport. In women's lacrosse, the addition of Maryland and Rutgers to the Big Ten brought the conference up to the requisite six participants, joining programs at Michigan, Northwestern, Ohio State and Penn State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lacrosse_and_JHU_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lacrosse_and_JHU-50">[37]</a></sup> In men's lacrosse, Ohio State and Penn State were the only existing participants. Coincident with the addition of Maryland and Rutgers, Michigan agreed to upgrade its successful club team to varsity status, giving the Big Ten five sponsoring schools, one short of the minimum six for an automatic bid. <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> opted to join the conference as its first affiliate member beginning in 2014. Johns Hopkins had been independent in men's lacrosse for 130 years, claiming 44 national championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JHU-hub_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-JHU-hub-51">[38]</a></sup> As long-time independents joined conferences (for example, Syracuse joining the Atlantic Coast Conference), other schools competing as independents in some cases concluded that the inability to earn an automatic bid to the NCAA tournament was becoming a more serious competitive disadvantage in scheduling and recruiting.</p>
<p>On March 23, 2016, the Big Ten Conference and Notre Dame announced the <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's ice hockey">Fighting Irish</a> would become a men's ice hockey affiliate beginning with the 2017-18 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[39]</a></sup> Notre Dame's team is currently a member of <a href="/wiki/Hockey_East" title="Hockey East">Hockey East</a>, and the move will save them from longer trips to <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> while renewing rivalries that existed in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">CCHA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">WCHA</a>.</p>
<p>In 2012, the conference announced it would move its headquarters from its location in <a href="/wiki/Park_Ridge,_Illinois" title="Park Ridge, Illinois">Park Ridge, Illinois</a> to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Rosemont,_Illinois" title="Rosemont, Illinois">Rosemont</a> by the end of 2013. The new office building is situated within Rosemont's MB Financial Entertainment District, alongside <a href="/wiki/Interstate_294" title="Interstate 294">Interstate 294</a>. The move into the building was finalized on October 14, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commissioners">Commissioners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Commissioners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The office of the commissioner of athletics was created in 1922 "to study athletic problems of the various member universities and assist in enforcing the eligibility rules which govern Big Ten athletics."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-traditions_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-traditions-26">[13]</a></sup></p>

<p><br/></p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Academic_Alliance" title="Big Ten Academic Alliance">Big Ten Academic Alliance</a></div>
<p>Twelve of the thirteen <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public schools</a> in the Big Ten (Nebraska excepted) are considered "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Ivies" title="Public Ivies">Public Ivies</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[43]</a></sup> (.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[45]</a></sup> Each Big Ten institution (Nebraska excepted) is a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Universities" title="American Association of Universities">American Association of Universities</a> and is ranked in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" title="US News &amp; World Report">US News &amp; World Report</a></i> top-100 and the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> top-200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[46]</a></sup> Nebraska joined the AAU in 1909 but was removed in April 2011 when the AAU disallowed <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska_Medical_Center" title="University of Nebraska Medical Center">University of Nebraska Medical Center</a> data points to be included in the AAU formula and began to decrease the weight given to agricultural research. Commissioner Jim Delany stated that Nebraska's removal from the AAU would have no bearing upon their Big Ten membership. Nebraska does, however, lead the NCAA with a record of 314 Academic All-Americans (followed by Notre Dame with 221).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[48]</a></sup> Currently, no Division I conference is composed exclusively of AAU members. However, the <a href="/wiki/University_Athletic_Association" title="University Athletic Association">University Athletic Association</a>, a Division III conference is composed of entirely AAU members.</p>
<p>All Big Ten members are members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Academic_Alliance" title="Big Ten Academic Alliance">Big Ten Academic Alliance</a> (BTAA), formerly known as the Committee on Institutional Cooperation (CIC), an academic consortium which allows students at Big Ten institutions to take distance courses at other participating institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[49]</a></sup> Students at participating schools are also allowed "in-house" viewing privileges at other participating schools' libraries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[50]</a></sup> The BTAA also employs collective purchasing, which has saved member institutions $19 million to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[51]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, a former Big Ten Conference member, was a member of the CIC from 1958 to June 29, 2016 (when it was renamed the Big Ten Academic Alliance).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btaa_chicago_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-btaa_chicago-65">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools_ranked_by_revenue">Schools ranked by revenue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Schools ranked by revenue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The schools below are listed by conference rank of total revenue. Total revenue includes ticket sales, contributions and donations, rights/licensing, student fees, school funds and all other sources including TV income, camp income, food and novelties. Total expenses includes coaching/staff, scholarships, buildings/ground, maintenance, utilities and rental fees and all other costs including recruiting, team travel, equipment and uniforms, conference dues and insurance costs. Surplus (or deficit) is calculated using the total revenue and total expenses data provided by <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>, individual institutions and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">United States Department of Education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[54]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_Athlete_of_the_Year">Big Ten Athlete of the Year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Big Ten Athlete of the Year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Athlete_of_the_Year" title="Big Ten Athlete of the Year">Big Ten Athlete of the Year</a> award is given annually to the athletes voted as the top male and female athlete in the Big Ten Conference.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_Medal_of_Honor">Big Ten Medal of Honor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Big Ten Medal of Honor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Medal_of_Honor" title="Big Ten Medal of Honor">Big Ten Medal of Honor</a> (annual; at each school; one male <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Student-athlete" title="Student-athlete">scholar-athlete</a> and one female scholar-athlete)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[57]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Big Ten Sportsmanship Award (annual; at each school; one male <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Student-athlete" title="Student-athlete">student-athlete</a> and one female student-athlete)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[58]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NACDA_Learfield_Sports_Directors.27_Cup_Rankings">NACDA Learfield Sports Directors' Cup Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: NACDA Learfield Sports Directors' Cup Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/NACDA_Directors%27_Cup" title="NACDA Directors' Cup">NACDA Learfield Sports Directors' Cup</a> is an annual award given by the National Association of Collegiate Directors of Athletics to the U.S. colleges and universities with the most success in collegiate athletics. Big Ten universities typically finish ranked in the top-50 of the final Directors' Cup annual rankings.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.932015_Capital_One_Cup_Standings">2014–2015 Capital One Cup Standings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2014–2015 Capital One Cup Standings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Capital_One_Cup_(college_sports)" title="Capital One Cup (college sports)">Capital One Cup</a> is an award given annually to the best men's and women's Division I college athletics programs in the United States. Points are earned throughout the year based on final standings of NCAA Championships and final coaches' poll rankings.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.932015_CBS_Sports_Best_in_College_Sports_Rankings">2014–2015 CBS Sports Best in College Sports Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2014–2015 CBS Sports Best in College Sports Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(October 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The CBS Sports Best in College Sports award is weighed more heavily toward sports that generate fan and media interest. The poll rates five sports: football, men's basketball, women's basketball, baseball and a "wild card" sport. The wild-card spot is awarded to the most successful among schools' other spectator sports: softball, men's lacrosse, men's ice hockey, men's soccer, wrestling, volleyball, women's soccer or women's gymnastics. Women's basketball, baseball, and the "wild card" carry normal weight, with men's basketball double and football triple.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conference_records">Conference records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Conference records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="NCAA_national_titles">NCAA national titles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: NCAA national titles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Through the sports year ended July 1, 2015, per published NCAA summary,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[60]</a></sup> with updates for the subsequent sports year.</p>
<p>Excluded from this list are all national championships earned <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletics_championship_game_outcomes" title="List of college athletics championship game outcomes">outside the scope of NCAA competition</a>, including <a href="/wiki/College_football_national_championships_in_NCAA_Division_I_FBS" title="College football national championships in NCAA Division I FBS">Division I FBS football titles</a>, women's <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women_championships" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women championships">AIAW championships</a> (17), <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Equestrian_Association" title="National Collegiate Equestrian Association">equestrian titles</a> (0), and retroactive <a href="/wiki/Helms_Athletic_Foundation" title="Helms Athletic Foundation">Helms Athletic Foundation titles</a>.</p>

<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^</a></b></span> Johns Hopkins was added in 2014 as an associate member that competed in men's lacrosse only. Johns Hopkins also began competing as an associate member in women's lacrosse in the 2016–17 school year.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2"><b><a href="#ref_2">^</a></b></span> Maryland won 192 conference championships as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC), second most in ACC history.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_3"><b><a href="#ref_3">^</a></b></span> Nebraska won 80 conference championships as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>, second most in Big 12 history. Nebraska also won 230 conference championships as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Eight_Conference" title="Big Eight Conference">Big Eight Conference</a>, the most in Big 8 history.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_4"><b><a href="#ref_4">^</a></b></span> Penn State won or shared 70 conference championships as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a> (1982–91) and earlier when it was known as the Eastern 8 Conference (1976–79).</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_5"><b><a href="#ref_5">^</a></b></span> Rutgers won six conference championships as a member of the Middle Three Conference, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Atlantic_Conference" title="Middle Atlantic Conference">Middle Atlantic Conference</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">original Big East Conference</a>, and both of its offshoots, the current non-football <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a>. (In 2013–14, Rutgers was a full member of The American, but housed its teams in field hockey and men's and women's lacrosse in the reconfigured Big East.)</li>
</ol>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Big_Ten_Conference_football_standings_(1959%E2%80%93present)" title="List of Big Ten Conference football standings (1959–present)">List of Big Ten Conference football standings (1959–present)</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_Big_Ten_Conference_football_season" title="2016 Big Ten Conference football season">2016 Big Ten Conference football season</a></div>
<p>When Maryland and Rutgers joined the Big Ten in 2014, the division names were changed to "East" and "West", with Purdue and the six schools in the Central Time Zone in the West and Indiana joining the remaining six <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">Eastern Time Zone</a> schools in the East. The only protected cross-division game is Indiana–Purdue. Beginning in 2016, the Big Ten adopted a nine-game conference schedule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_divisions_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014_divisions-49">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[63]</a></sup> Also since 2016, the Big Ten no longer allows its members to play <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="Football Championship Subdivision">Football Championship Subdivision</a> teams, and also requires at least one non-conference game against a school in the <a href="/wiki/Power_Five_conferences" title="Power Five conferences">Power Five conferences</a> (<a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pac-12_Conference" title="Pac-12 Conference">Pac-12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">SEC</a>). At the time this policy was first announced, games against <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_independent_schools" title="NCAA Division I FBS independent schools">FBS independents</a> <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame</a> and <a href="/wiki/BYU_Cougars_football" title="BYU Cougars football">BYU</a> would automatically count toward the Power Five requirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGuire_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-McGuire-77">[64]</a></sup> Additionally, Big Ten teams that were already under contract to play teams in the "Group of Five" leagues (<a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conference_USA" title="Conference USA">C-USA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mid-American_Conference" title="Mid-American Conference">MAC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_West_Conference" title="Mountain West Conference">MW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Belt_Conference" title="Sun Belt Conference">Sun Belt</a>) were allowed to honor those contracts. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, three Big Ten members had American member <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bearcats_football" title="Cincinnati Bearcats football">Cincinnati</a> on their future schedules, one had fellow American member <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Huskies_football" title="Connecticut Huskies football">Connecticut</a> on its future schedule; and one had future games scheduled against both. ESPN, citing a Big Ten executive, reported in 2015 that the Big Ten would allow exceptions to the Power Five rule on a case-by-case basis, and also that the other FBS independent at that time, <a href="/wiki/Army_Black_Knights_football" title="Army Black Knights football">Army</a>, had been added to the list of non-Power Five schools that would automatically be counted as Power Five opponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[65]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">
<tr>
<th style="background:#fd7">West Division</th>

</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Ten_Conference_Champions">Big Ten Conference Champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Big Ten Conference Champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Big_Ten_Conference_football_champions" title="List of Big Ten Conference football champions">List of Big Ten Conference football champions</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Football_Championship_Game" title="Big Ten Football Championship Game">Big Ten Football Championship Game</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bowl_games">Bowl games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Bowl games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1946, the Big Ten champion has had a tie-in with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(game)" title="Rose Bowl (game)">Rose Bowl game</a>. Michigan appeared in the first <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">bowl game</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1902_Rose_Bowl" title="1902 Rose Bowl">1902 Rose Bowl</a>. After that, the Big Ten did not allow their schools to participate in bowl games, until the agreement struck with the Pacific Coast Conference for the <a href="/wiki/1947_Rose_Bowl" title="1947 Rose Bowl">1947 Rose Bowl</a>. From 1946 through 1971, the Big Ten did not allow the same team to represent the conference in consecutive years in the Rose Bowl with an exception made after the 1961 season in which Minnesota played in the <a href="/wiki/1962_Rose_Bowl" title="1962 Rose Bowl">1962 Rose Bowl</a> after playing in the <a href="/wiki/1961_Rose_Bowl" title="1961 Rose Bowl">1961 Rose Bowl</a> due to Ohio State declining the bid because of Ohio State faculty concerns about academics. Due to their "Rose Bowl or bust" policy, the 1972, 1973 and 1974 Michigan squads did not play in bowl games despite posting 10 wins in each season.</p>
<p>It was not until the 1975 season that the Big Ten allowed teams to play in bowl games other than the Rose Bowl. Michigan, which had been shut out of the postseason the previous three years, was the first beneficiary of the new rule when it played in the Orange Bowl vs. Oklahoma. Due to the pre-1975 rules, Big Ten teams such as Michigan and Ohio State have lower numbers of all-time bowl appearances than powerhouse teams from the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a> (previously Big Eight and Southwest Conferences) and <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a>, which always placed multiple teams in bowl games every year.</p>
<p>Starting in the 2014–15 season, a new slate of bowl game selections will include several new bowl games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[66]</a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bowl_selection_procedures">Bowl selection procedures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Bowl selection procedures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although the pick order usually corresponds to the conference standings, the bowls are not required to make their choices strictly according to the won-lost records; many factors influence bowl selections, especially the likely turnout of the team's fans. Picks are made after CFP selections; the bowl with the #2 pick will have the first pick of the remaining teams in the conference.</p>
<p>For all non-College Football Playoff partners, the bowl partner will request a Big Ten team. The Big Ten will approve or assign another team based on internal selection parameters.</p>
<p>When not hosting a semifinal, the Capital One Orange Bowl will select the highest-ranked team from the Big Ten, SEC or Notre Dame to face an ACC opponent. The Big Ten Champion cannot play in the Orange Bowl. If a Big Ten team is not selected by the Orange Bowl, the Buffalo Wild Wings Citrus Bowl will submit a request for a Big Ten team.</p>
<p>The Outback, Foster Farms and Holiday Bowls will feature at least five different Big Ten schools over the six-year agreement (through 2019 season). The Music City and Taxslayer Bowl will coordinate their selections allowing only one to pick a Big Ten team. The Big Ten will make appearances in three of each bowl games over the term of the agreement (through 2019 season).</p>
<p>The New Era Pinstripe Bowl will feature a minimum of six different Big Ten teams over the eight-year agreement (through 2021 season).</p>
<p>The Quick Lane, Armed Forces and Heart of Dallas Bowls will select a bowl-eligible Big Ten team, subject to conference approval. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_coach_compensation">Head coach compensation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Head coach compensation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marching_bands">Marching bands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Marching bands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All Big Ten member schools have <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching bands</a> which perform regularly during the football season. Ten of fourteen member schools have won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sudler_Trophy" title="Sudler Trophy">Sudler Trophy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sudler_Trophy_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sudler_Trophy-88">[75]</a></sup> generally considered the most prestigious honor a collegiate marching band can receive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sudler_prestige_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sudler_prestige-89">[76]</a></sup> The first three Sudler trophies were awarded to Big Ten marching bands—<a href="/wiki/Michigan_Marching_Band" title="Michigan Marching Band">Michigan</a> (1982), <a href="/wiki/Marching_Illini" title="Marching Illini">Illinois</a> (1983) and <a href="/wiki/The_Ohio_State_University_Marching_Band" title="The Ohio State University Marching Band">Ohio State</a> (1984).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sudler_Trophy_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sudler_Trophy-88">[75]</a></sup> The Big Ten also has more Sudler Trophy recipients than any other collegiate athletic conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sudler_Trophy_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sudler_Trophy-88">[75]</a></sup> It is a longstanding tradition for Big Ten bands to perform the opposing team's fight song during their pregame performance.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conference_individual_honors">Conference individual honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Conference individual honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference_football_individual_honors" title="Big Ten Conference football individual honors">Big Ten Conference football individual honors</a></div>
<p>Coaches and media of the Big Ten Conference award individual honors at the end of each football season.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Men's basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Big_Ten_Conference_men%27s_basketball_season" title="2016–17 Big Ten Conference men's basketball season">2016–17 Big Ten Conference men's basketball season</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="Big Ten Conference Men's Basketball Tournament">Big Ten Conference Men's Basketball Tournament</a></div>
<p>The Big Ten has participated in basketball since 1904, and has led the nation in attendance every season since 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[77]</a></sup> It has been a national powerhouse in <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">men's basketball</a>, having multiple championship winners and often sending four or more teams to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Men's Basketball Tournament</a>. Previous NCAA champions include Indiana with five titles, Michigan State with two, and Wisconsin, Michigan, and Ohio State with one each. Maryland, which joined the Big Ten in 2014, won one NCAA championship as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[79]</a></sup> Ohio State played in the first NCAA tournament national championship game in 1939, losing to Oregon. Despite this, Jimmy Hull of Ohio State was the first NCAA tournament MVP. The first three tournament MVPs came from the Big Ten (Marv Huffman of Indiana in 1940 and John Katz of Wisconsin in 1941).</p>
<p>Big Ten teams have also experienced success in the postseason <a href="/wiki/National_Invitation_Tournament" title="National Invitation Tournament">NIT</a>. Since 1974, 13 Big Ten teams have made it to the championship game, winning nine championships. Michigan, Ohio State, and Minnesota have won two NIT championships, while Indiana, Penn State, and Purdue have won one each. Two other current members, Maryland and Nebraska, won NIT titles before they joined the Big Ten. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Helms_Athletic_Foundation" title="Helms Athletic Foundation">Helms Athletic Foundation</a> recognizes Illinois as the 1915 National Champions, Minnesota as the 1902 and 1919 National Champions, Northwestern as the 1931 National Champion, Purdue as the 1932 National Champions, and Wisconsin as the 1912, 1914 and 1916 National Champions. Former member Chicago won a post-season national championship series in 1908.</p>
<p>Since 1999, the Big Ten has taken part in the <a href="/wiki/ACC%E2%80%93Big_Ten_Challenge" title="ACC–Big Ten Challenge">ACC–Big Ten Challenge</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a>. The ACC holds a 10–4–2 record against the Big Ten; Minnesota, Nebraska, Purdue, and Rutgers are the only Big Ten schools without losing records in the challenge.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="All-time_school_records_2">All-time school records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: All-time school records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Big_Ten_Conference_men%27s_basketball_regular_season_champions" title="List of Big Ten Conference men's basketball regular season champions">List of Big Ten Conference men's basketball regular season champions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="Big Ten Conference Men's Basketball Tournament">Big Ten Conference Men's Basketball Tournament</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_basketball">Women's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Women's basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Women's basketball teams have played a total of ten times in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Women's Division I Basketball Championship</a> (since 1982) and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Invitation_Tournament" title="Women's National Invitation Tournament">Women's National Invitation Tournament Championship</a> (since 1998). Purdue is the only current Big Ten member to have won the NCAA women's basketball national title while a member of the conference. Both schools that joined in 2014, Maryland and Rutgers, won national titles before joining the Big Ten—Rutgers won the final <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association of Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">AIAW</a> <a href="/wiki/AIAW_Women%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="AIAW Women's Basketball Tournament">championship</a> in 1982, when it was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Eastern 8</a>, and Maryland won the NCAA title in 2006 as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a>. Big Ten women's basketball led conference attendance from 1993 to 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like the men's teams, the women's basketball teams in the Big Ten participate in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Ten%E2%80%93ACC_Women%27s_Challenge" title="Big Ten–ACC Women's Challenge">Big Ten–ACC Women's Challenge</a>, which was founded in 2007.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_championships.2C_Final_Fours.2C_and_NCAA_tournament_appearances_2">National championships, Final Fours, and NCAA tournament appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: National championships, Final Fours, and NCAA tournament appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Field_hockey">Field hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Field hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Big Ten field hockey programs have won 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Field_Hockey_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Field Hockey Championship">NCAA Championships</a>, although only two of these titles were won by schools as Big Ten members. Maryland won eight national championships as a member of the ACC, second most in the sport all-time. Penn State's two AIAW championships were also won before it became a Big Ten member and before the NCAA sponsored women's sports.</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center;">
<tr>
<th style="width:105px;">School</th>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_gymnastics">Men's gymnastics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Men's gymnastics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Big Ten fields seven of the remaining fifteen Division I men's gymnastics teams. In 2014, Michigan edged out Oklahoma for their 6th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Gymnastics_championship" title="NCAA Men's Gymnastics championship">NCAA Men's Gymnastics championship</a>, the school's third in five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[81]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_ice_hockey">Men's ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Men's ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Big Ten began sponsoring men's <a href="/wiki/College_ice_hockey" title="College ice hockey">ice hockey</a> in the 2013–14 season. The inaugural season includes 6 schools: <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Michigan Wolverines men's ice hockey">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Michigan State Spartans men's ice hockey">Michigan State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Ohio State Buckeyes men's ice hockey">Ohio State</a> joined from the disbanded <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">CCHA</a>; <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers men's ice hockey">Minnesota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Wisconsin Badgers men's ice hockey">Wisconsin</a> joined from the <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">WCHA</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Nittany_Lions_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Penn State Nittany Lions men's ice hockey">Penn State</a> joined after playing its first NCAA Division I season (2012–2013) as an independent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Men.27s_Ice_Hockey_To_Be_Recommended_As_Official_Big_Ten_Sport_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Men.27s_Ice_Hockey_To_Be_Recommended_As_Official_Big_Ten_Sport-98">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Ten_Officially_Announces_Hockey_Conference_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Ten_Officially_Announces_Hockey_Conference-99">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">Notre Dame</a> will be joining the league in 2017.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the conclusion of each regular season schedule the coaches of each Big Ten team, as well as a media panel, vote which players they choose to be on the three All-Conference Teams:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[84]</a></sup> first team, second team and rookie team. Additionally they vote to award the 5 individual trophies to an eligible player at the same time. The Big Ten also awards a Tournament Most Outstanding Player which is voted on after the conclusion of the conference tournament. Each team also names one of their players to be honored for the conference Sportsmanship Award. All of the awards were created for the inaugural season (<a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_ice_hockey_season" title="2013–14 NCAA Division I men's ice hockey season">2013–14</a>).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_lacrosse">Men's lacrosse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Men's lacrosse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Big Ten began sponsoring men's <a href="/wiki/College_lacrosse" title="College lacrosse">lacrosse</a> in the 2015 season. The Big Ten lacrosse league includes <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Maryland Terrapins men's lacrosse">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Michigan Wolverines men's lacrosse">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Ohio State Buckeyes men's lacrosse">Ohio State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Nittany_Lions_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Penn State Nittany Lions men's lacrosse">Penn State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Rutgers Scarlet Knights men's lacrosse">Rutgers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays men's lacrosse">Johns Hopkins</a>, which joined the Big Ten conference as an affiliate member in 2014. The teams that compete in Big Ten men's lacrosse have combined to win 11 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Lacrosse Championship">NCAA national championships</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Ten_Announces_Institution_of_Men.27s_and_Women.27s_Lacrosse_and_Addition_of_Johns_Hopkins_as_Men.27s_Lacrosse_Sport_Affiliate_Member_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Ten_Announces_Institution_of_Men.27s_and_Women.27s_Lacrosse_and_Addition_of_Johns_Hopkins_as_Men.27s_Lacrosse_Sport_Affiliate_Member-102">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the addition of Johns Hopkins and Maryland to the league, Big Ten men's lacrosse boasts two of the top programs and most heated rivals in the history of the sport. Johns Hopkins (29) and Maryland (24) combine for 53 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Lacrosse Championship">NCAA Men's Lacrosse</a> Final Four appearances. The media and both schools have called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins-Maryland_rivalry" title="Johns Hopkins-Maryland rivalry">Johns Hopkins–Maryland rivalry</a> the greatest and most historic rivalry in men's lacrosse. Since 1895, the two teams have matched up more than 100 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jhu_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-jhu-103">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2008preview_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-2008preview-104">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[88]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_lacrosse">Women's lacrosse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Women's lacrosse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Tournament" title="Big Ten Conference Women's Lacrosse Tournament">Big Ten Conference Women's Lacrosse Tournament</a></div>
<p>Women's <a href="/wiki/College_lacrosse" title="College lacrosse">lacrosse</a> became a Big Ten-sponsored sport in the 2015 season. The Big Ten women's lacrosse league includes <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays women's lacrosse">Johns Hopkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Maryland Terrapins women's lacrosse">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines" title="Michigan Wolverines">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Northwestern Wildcats women's lacrosse">Northwestern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes" title="Ohio State Buckeyes">Ohio State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Nittany_Lions" title="Penn State Nittany Lions">Penn State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights" title="Rutgers Scarlet Knights">Rutgers</a>. Big Ten women's lacrosse programs have 21 of the 34 all-time NCAA championships, including 10 of the last 11. Maryland has won 13 NCAA national championships, including seven straight from 1995 to 2001 and most recently in 2015. Northwestern has claimed seven NCAA titles, including five straight from 2005 to 2009. Penn State has earned three pre-NCAA national titles and two NCAA titles in 1987 and 1989. Johns Hopkins became the seventh women's lacrosse program in the Big Ten as of July 1, 2016.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_soccer">Men's soccer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Men's soccer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Big Ten men's soccer league includes <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Hoosiers_men%27s_soccer" title="Indiana Hoosiers men's soccer">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_soccer" title="Maryland Terrapins men's soccer">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines_men%27s_soccer" title="Michigan Wolverines men's soccer">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_soccer" title="Michigan State Spartans men's soccer">Michigan State</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_men%27s_soccer" title="Northwestern Wildcats men's soccer">Northwestern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_men%27s_soccer" title="Ohio State Buckeyes men's soccer">Ohio State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Nittany_Lions_men%27s_soccer" title="Penn State Nittany Lions men's soccer">Penn State</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights_men%27s_soccer" title="Rutgers Scarlet Knights men's soccer">Rutgers</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_soccer" title="Wisconsin Badgers men's soccer">Wisconsin</a>. Big Ten men's soccer programs have combined to win 14 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Soccer_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Soccer Championship">NCAA national championships</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Big_Ten_Conference_football_rivalry_games" title="List of Big Ten Conference football rivalry games">List of Big Ten Conference football rivalry games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana%E2%80%93Purdue_rivalry" title="Indiana–Purdue rivalry">Indiana–Purdue rivalry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan%E2%80%93Ohio_State_football_rivalry" title="Michigan–Ohio State football rivalry">Michigan–Ohio State football rivalry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota%E2%80%93Wisconsin_football_rivalry" title="Minnesota–Wisconsin football rivalry">Minnesota–Wisconsin football rivalry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State%E2%80%93Penn_State_football_rivalry" title="Ohio State–Penn State football rivalry">Ohio State–Penn State football rivalry</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intra-Conference_Football_Rivalries">Intra-Conference Football Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Intra-Conference Football Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The members of the Big Ten have longstanding rivalries with each other, especially on the football field. Each school, except Maryland and Rutgers, has at least one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traveling_trophy" title="Traveling trophy">traveling trophy</a> at stake.
