<td><a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame%E2%80%93Purdue_football_rivalry" title="Notre Dame–Purdue football rivalry">Notre Dame–Purdue football rivalry</a></td>
<td>Shillelagh Trophy</td>
<td>86</td>
<td>26–58–2</td>
<td>Notre Dame</td>
<td>Purdue lost 7</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-College_Football_Data_Warehouse_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-College_Football_Data_Warehouse-106">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1993 through 2010, the Big Ten football schedule was set up with each team having two permanent matches within the conference, with the other eight teams in the conference rotating out of the schedule in pairs for two-year stints. Permanent matches were as follows:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Illinois</b>: Indiana, Northwestern</li>
<li><b>Indiana</b>: Illinois, Purdue</li>
<li><b>Iowa</b>: Minnesota, Wisconsin</li>
<li><b>Michigan</b>: Michigan State, Ohio State</li>
<li><b>Michigan State</b>: Michigan, Penn State</li>
<li><b>Minnesota</b>: Iowa, Wisconsin</li>
<li><b>Northwestern</b>: Illinois, Purdue</li>
<li><b>Ohio State</b>: Michigan, Penn State</li>
<li><b>Penn State</b>: Michigan State, Ohio State</li>
<li><b>Purdue</b>: Indiana, Northwestern</li>
<li><b>Wisconsin</b>: Iowa, Minnesota</li>
</ul>
<p>This system was discontinued after the 2010 season, as teams became grouped into two divisions, and would play all teams in their division once, with one protected cross-over game, and two games rotating against the other five opponents from the opposing division.</p>
<p>Most of the above permanent rivalries were maintained. By virtue of the new alignment, a handful of new permanent divisional opponents were created, as all pairs of teams within the same division would face off each season. Furthermore, three new permanent inter-divisional matches resulted from the realignment: Purdue–Iowa, Michigan State–Indiana, and Penn State–Nebraska. The following past permanent matches were maintained across divisions: Minnesota–Wisconsin, Michigan–Ohio State, and Illinois–Northwestern.</p>
<p>The new alignment, however, caused some of the above permanent rivalries to be discontinued. These were: Iowa–Wisconsin, Northwestern–Purdue, and Michigan State–Penn State. These matchups would continue to be played, but only twice every five years on average. More rivalries were disrupted, and some resumed on a yearly basis, when the league realigned into East and West Divisions for the 2014 season with the addition of Maryland and Rutgers. The two new schools were placed in the new East Division with Penn State, and the two Indiana schools were divided (Indiana to the East and Purdue to the West). With the move to a nine-game conference schedule in 2016, all cross-division games will be held at least once in a four-year cycle except for Indiana–Purdue, which is the only protected cross-division game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_realignment_approved_48-3"><a href="#cite_note-2014_realignment_approved-48">[35]</a></sup> The conference later announced that once the new scheduling format takes effect in 2016, members will be prohibited from playing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="Football Championship Subdivision">FCS</a> teams, and required to play at least one non-conference game against a team in the <a href="/wiki/Power_Five_conferences" title="Power Five conferences">Power Five conferences</a> (<a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pac-12_Conference" title="Pac-12 Conference">Pac-12</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">SEC</a>; presumably, this would also allow for non-conference games against Big Ten opponents that are not on the conference schedule). Games against <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_independent_schools" title="NCAA Division I FBS independent schools">independents</a> <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame</a> (an ACC member in non-football sports) and <a href="/wiki/BYU_Cougars_football" title="BYU Cougars football">BYU</a> will also count toward the Power Five requirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGuire_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-McGuire-77">[64]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extra-conference_rivalries">Extra-conference rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Extra-conference rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Three Big Ten teams—Purdue, Michigan State and Michigan—had rivalries in football with <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football_rivalries" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football rivalries">Notre Dame</a>. After the University of Southern California with 35 wins (including a vacated 2005 win), the Michigan State Spartans have the most wins against the Irish, with 28. The Purdue Boilermakers follow with 26, and Michigan ranks fourth all-time with 24.</p>
<p>Penn State has a longstanding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitt%E2%80%93Penn_State_rivalry" title="Pitt–Penn State rivalry">rivalry</a> with <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">Pittsburgh</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a>, but the two schools did not meet from 2000 until renewing the rivalry with an alternating home-and-home series from 2016 to 2019. Penn State also has long histories with independent <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame</a>; <a href="/wiki/Temple_Owls_football" title="Temple Owls football">Temple</a> of <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">The American</a>; <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_football" title="Syracuse Orange football">Syracuse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_College_Eagles_football" title="Boston College Eagles football">Boston College</a> of the ACC; and <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Mountaineers_football" title="West Virginia Mountaineers football">West Virginia</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>. Additionally, Penn State maintains strong intrastate rivalries with <a href="/wiki/Patriot_League" title="Patriot League">Patriot League</a> universities <a href="/wiki/Bucknell_Bison" title="Bucknell Bison">Bucknell</a> in men's basketball and men's lacrosse, and <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Mountain_Hawks" title="Lehigh Mountain Hawks">Lehigh</a> in wrestling. Most of these rivalries were cultivated while Penn State operated independent of conference affiliation; the constraints of playing a full conference schedule, especially in football, have reduced the number of meetings between Penn State and its non-Big Ten rivals.</p>
<p>Iowa has an in-state rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Iowa_State_Cyclones" title="Iowa State Cyclones">Iowa State</a> of the Big 12, with the winner getting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cy-Hawk_Trophy" title="Cy-Hawk Trophy">Cy-Hawk Trophy</a> in football. Iowa and Iowa State also compete annually in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hy-Vee_Cy-Hawk_Series" title="Hy-Vee Cy-Hawk Series">Cy-Hawk Series</a> sponsored by Hy-Vee (as of 2011 this series is now sponsored by The Iowa Corngrowers Association), the competition includes all head-to-head regular season competitions in all sports. Iowa also holds rivalries in basketball with the state's other two Division I programs, <a href="/wiki/Drake_Bulldogs" title="Drake Bulldogs">Drake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Iowa_Panthers" title="Northern Iowa Panthers">Northern Iowa</a>.</p>
<p>Indiana has an out-of-conference rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats" title="Kentucky Wildcats">Kentucky</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">SEC</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Indiana%E2%80%93Kentucky_rivalry" title="Indiana–Kentucky rivalry">Indiana–Kentucky rivalry</a>). While the two schools played in football for many years, the rivalry was rooted in their decades of national success in men's basketball. The two no longer play one another in football, but their basketball rivalry continued until a dispute about game sites ended the series after 2011. In the last season of the rivalry (2011–12), the teams played twice. During the regular season, then-unranked <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Indiana_Hoosiers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2011–12 Indiana Hoosiers men's basketball team">Indiana</a> defeated then-#1 ranked <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2011–12 Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball team">Kentucky</a> 73–72 at Assembly Hall. The Wildcats avenged the loss in the NCAA tournament, defeating Indiana 102–90 in the South Regional final in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Dome" title="Georgia Dome">Atlanta</a> on their way to a national title. The teams next played in the 2016 NCAA tournament, with Indiana winning.</p>
<p>Illinois has a longstanding basketball rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">SEC</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Tigers_men%27s_basketball" title="Missouri Tigers men's basketball">Missouri Tigers</a>, with the two men's teams squaring off annually in the "<a href="/wiki/Braggin%27_Rights" title="Braggin' Rights">Braggin' Rights</a>" game. It has been held in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a> since 1980, first at the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Arena" title="St. Louis Arena">St. Louis Arena</a> and since 1994 at the <a href="/wiki/Scottrade_Center" title="Scottrade Center">Scottrade Center</a>. This rivalry has been carried over into football as "The Arch Rivalry" with games played at the <a href="/wiki/The_Dome_at_America%27s_Center" title="The Dome at America's Center">Edward Jones Dome</a> in St. Louis in 2002 and 2003 and four games in 2007 through 2010.<a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.stlouissports.org/pressbox/releases/missouriillinois82505.php" rel="nofollow">[3]</a></p>
<p>Wisconsin has a long-standing in-state basketball rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Marquette_Golden_Eagles_men%27s_basketball" title="Marquette Golden Eagles men's basketball">Marquette</a>. The series has intensified as of late with both teams having made the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Final Four</a> in recent years. The schools also played an annual football game before Marquette abandoned its football program in 1961. The school also has minor rivalries in basketball with the two other Division I members of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin_System" title="University of Wisconsin System">University of Wisconsin System</a>, which include the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Panthers" title="Milwaukee Panthers">University of Wisconsin–Milwaukee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Phoenix" title="Green Bay Phoenix">University of Wisconsin–Green Bay</a>.</p>
<p>Minnesota men's ice hockey has a prolific and fierce border rivalry with the University of North Dakota. The two teams played annually between 1948 and 2013 as members of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">Western Collegiate Hockey Association</a> prior to the inception of the Big Ten Conference. The rivalry will resume in 2016 in non-conference action.</p>
<p>In the early days of the Big Ten, the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Maroons_football" title="Chicago Maroons football">Chicago</a>–<a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines_football" title="Michigan Wolverines football">Michigan</a> game was played on <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving</a>, usually with conference championship implications and was considered one of the first major rivalries of the conference.</p>
<p>Also in the early days of the conference, and at <a href="/wiki/Knute_Rockne" title="Knute Rockne">Knute Rockne</a>'s insistence, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_football" title="Northwestern Wildcats football">Northwestern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame</a> had a yearly contest, with the winner taking home a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shillelagh_(weapon)" title="Shillelagh (weapon)">shillelagh</a>, much like the winner of the <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_football" title="USC Trojans football">USC</a>–Notre Dame and Purdue–Notre Dame contests now receive. The Northwestern–Notre Dame shillelagh was largely forgotten by the early 1960s and is now solely an element of college football's storied past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Big Ten is second to the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC) in football stadiums that seat over 100,000, with the Big Ten having three to the SEC's four. The Big Ten's 100,000-seat stadiums are Beaver Stadium, Michigan Stadium, and Ohio Stadium. Only five other college football stadium have such a capacity: <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Aggies_football" title="Texas A&amp;M Aggies football">Texas A&amp;M's</a> <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Field" title="Kyle Field">Kyle Field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neyland_Stadium" title="Neyland Stadium">Neyland Stadium</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Volunteers_football" title="Tennessee Volunteers football">University of Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryant%E2%80%93Denny_Stadium" title="Bryant–Denny Stadium">Bryant–Denny Stadium</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Crimson_Tide_football" title="Alabama Crimson Tide football">University of Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/LSU_Tigers_football" title="LSU Tigers football">LSU's</a> <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Stadium_(LSU)" title="Tiger Stadium (LSU)">Tiger Stadium</a> in the SEC, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darrell_K_Royal-Texas_Memorial_Stadium" title="Darrell K Royal-Texas Memorial Stadium">Darrell K Royal-Texas Memorial Stadium</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Longhorns_football" title="Texas Longhorns football">University of Texas at Austin</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>. The three stadiums are three of the four largest football stadiums in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_American_football_stadiums_by_capacity" title="List of American football stadiums by capacity">United States</a>, as well as the third, fourth, and seventh <a href="/wiki/List_of_stadiums_by_capacity" title="List of stadiums by capacity">largest sports stadiums in the world</a>.</p>
<p>The Big Ten is home to two of the top-10 largest on-campus basketball arenas in the country: Ohio State's <a href="/wiki/Value_City_Arena" title="Value City Arena">Value City Arena</a> and Maryland's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/XFINITY_Center_(College_Park,_Maryland)" title="XFINITY Center (College Park, Maryland)">XFINITY Center</a>. Additionally, arenas at Indiana, Wisconsin, Illinois, Iowa, and Penn State rank among the top-20 largest on-campus basketball facilities in the United States. The Big Ten Conference features more on-campus basketball arenas with seating capacities of 15,000 or more than any other conference in the country.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 2010, the Big Ten has carriage agreements with the following broadcast and cable networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast_television">Broadcast television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Broadcast television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/ESPN_on_ABC" title="ESPN on ABC">ESPN on ABC</a></b> broadcasts football games within the conference, primarily in the 3:30 p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Time" title="Eastern Time">ET</a>/2:30 p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">CT</a> slot on Saturdays, but occasionally at noon and during <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Football" title="Saturday Night Football">Saturday Night Football</a></i>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/CBS_Sports" title="CBS Sports">CBS Sports</a></b> carries select men's basketball games on weekends, including the semifinals and championship game of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="Big Ten Men's Basketball Tournament">Big Ten Men's Basketball Tournament</a>.</li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(USA)" title="Fox Sports (USA)">Fox Sports</a></b> carries the Big Ten football championship from the 2011 through 2016 seasons.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cable_television">Cable television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Big_Ten_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Cable television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Network" title="Big Ten Network">Big Ten Network</a></b> was created in 2006 through a joint partnership between the Big Ten and <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation" title="News Corporation">News Corporation</a> and debuted the following year, replacing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPN_Plus" title="ESPN Plus">ESPN Plus</a> package previously offered to Big Ten markets via syndication. Based in downtown Chicago, the network's lineup consists exclusively of Big Ten-related programming, such as a nightly highlights show, in addition to live events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/ESPN_Inc." title="ESPN Inc.">ESPN Inc.</a> –</b> Big Ten football, basketball and volleyball air on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN2" title="ESPN2">ESPN2</a>, and sometimes on <a href="/wiki/ESPNU" title="ESPNU">ESPNU</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Classic" title="ESPN Classic">ESPN Classic</a>. The conference's contract with ABC/ESPN also allows for the transmission of events through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPN_Mobile" title="ESPN Mobile">ESPN Mobile</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPN3.com" title="ESPN3.com">ESPN3.com</a>, and On Demand platforms.</li>
</ul>

<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.bigten.org/newlogo/" rel="nofollow">"Big Ten Conference Reveals New Logo and Honors Football History with Division Names and Trophies"</a>. Big Ten Conference<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 April</span> 2014</span>. <q>The new Big Ten logo was developed to symbolize the conference's future, as well as its rich heritage, strong tradition of competition, academic leadership, and passionate alumni", said Gericke. "Its contemporary collegiate lettering includes an embedded numeral "10" in the word "BIG", which allows fans to see "BIG" and "10" in a single word. Memorable and distinctive, the new logo evolved from the previous logo's use of negative space and is built on the conference's iconic name, without reference to the number of member institutions. The new logo also provides the flexibility of multiple versions which can be used horizontally, vertically and within new media.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABig+Ten+Conference&amp;rft.btitle=Big+Ten+Conference+Reveals+New+Logo+and+Honors+Football+History+with+Division+Names+and+Trophies&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bigten.org%2Fnewlogo%2F&amp;rft.pub=Big+Ten+Conference&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
